The instructions they provide consist of a couple of pictures on the package. However, these are very easy to replace. Just remember to orient the blade correctly when you drop them in. There are two little tabs on each blade that have to be oriented right. If the blade doesn't seem to sit correctly, turn them until they drop down. When you get a new Norelco razor or replace the blades on your current one you may not get the best shave for a week or two. It takes a while for the blades to \\"break-in. \\" As such, don't be disappointed if the first few shave with new blades do not seem as close and smooth as you expected. Give them a couple of weeks, they will improve.

  217. I purchased this product to replace the heads on my Philips Norelco 8160XLCC. It was the cheaper of the two replacement blade sets listed at Amazon.   671. I purchased the HQ9 heads from Amazon. Easy to find and order, package arrived in a week on the free shipping deal. Outstanding! Popped them into my shaver and was instantly rewarded with a close, comfortable shave. But it turns out I didn't need new cutter heads after all. I had been neglecting to properly clean my 14 month old Speed-XL shaver. What I thought was dulling cutters was actually a tremendous build-up of GUNK inside the cutter heads. I wish I could show you the pile of gunk I just cleaned-out! The triple track cutters have more sharp edges and corners in them that the earlier single track models (I've been a Norelco man for some 30 years now), and they trap and hold more gunk than ever before. They need to be cleaned-out more often. Once properly cleaned, my old cutter heads delivered a shave at like-new closeness and comfort. So guys, RTFM and follow the directions! Do a quick cleaning (hot tap water if you have a water cleanable model) about once a week. Once a month, sit down and remove the cutters and clean them thoroughly with the small brush they gave you. Be careful to not mix-up the combs and cutters! You can most likely save yourself the thirty bucks on new heads for another year or so, and keep getting that satisfying Norelco shave :)

  847. I upgraded to an HQ9 shaver a while ago from a lower end HQ8. I was never happy with the shave of the HQ9. It was supposed to be an upgrade over my cheaper HQ8 shaver with the HQ9 having a slightly faster, more powerful motor. The HQ9 heads are supposed to provide a faster shave over the HQ8 because of the larger cutting surface area. I did not find that be the case at all and it was also less comfortable.<br /><br />I finally discovered that the older, more traditional HQ8 heads actually fit in the HQ9 shaver. Upon making this change, I finally have my upgraded shaver. The combination of the more powerful motor with the traditional type head is the best for my skin. It's comfortable and shaves much faster. It's faster than my old HQ8 shaver and faster than the HQ9 shaver with the original HQ9 heads. To top it off, the HQ8 heads are cheaper too.<br /><br />I see two reasons for my experience. One is pointed out by a fellow reviewer. The use of additional rows reduces the surface area of the outermost row, which is the row that has the highest speed. Therefore, the design of the HQ9 head actually reduces the surface area of the highest speed cutting area. Second, the additional row of blades creates a larger area of drag for the motor. The HQ9 shaver actually has to work harder to turn the HQ9 heads.<br /><br />In short, try the HQ8 heads in your HQ9 razor the next time you need to replace them. I think you'll find it becomes a better shaver.

  1804. I recently purchased these replacement heads for my Philips Norelco Model 8240XL, after having previously purchased them on Amazon just shy of two years ago. That previous set endured daily use on my semi-heavy facial hair growth. I use my electric razor as a preshaver to remove my longer facial hair down to the stubble so that I can then obtain a completely smooth shave with a manual 4-blade razor. This method works for me, at least, and results in much less irritation because there is then far less chance of me catching or tugging the longer hairs with my manual razor.<br /><br />Unfortunately, whenever I have had to replace these heads, it has has been because a tiny blade of one of the cutters has broken off which subsequently prevents that damaged cutter, as well as the other undamaged two, from spinning. Unless you happen to have a spare set of these new replacement heads on hand or perhaps even a single leftover one from previous set, this can be problematic, since your razor will be rendered inoperable. Prior to receiving my most recent set of replacement heads, however, I was able to work around this issue by simply removing both the damaged cutter and its screen from the shaver so that the other two could still spin and be used (trying to avoid the open hole left by the removed cutter and screen, of course).<br /><br />Philips Norelo recommends replacing these heads once per year to obtain the best possible shave but I have typically been able to use them for twice that amount of time without much noticeable difference in shave quality.<br /><br />I have only given these replacement heads three stars because I personally wish that they could provide me with a much closer and smoother shave without having to use it in conjunction with a manual razor. Also, the cost of these heads seems borderline outrageous when you consider what you are actually getting for the price. I'm particularly astonished that they have increased 30% in price, since the last time Ipurchased them exactly two years ago in 2011.<br /><br />UPDATE (1/1/2015): I have now decided to stop purchasing these HQ9 replacement heads for my Philips Norelco Model 8240XL because the price for such continues to escalate astronomically. After some online research, I have learned that the [[ASIN:B000068PBT Philips Norelco HQ8 Dual Precision Replacement Heads]]replacement heads will also actually work on my older shaver, despite that fact not being indicated by the manufacturer.
